Reinforcing Argument: Diameters and Semicircles
Reinforces the refutation using diameters and semicircles to show impossibility of actual infinity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the concept of diameters and semicircles is used to argue against the possibility of an actual infinite series of orbits.

Core Idea
Potential infinity of orbits would entail actual infinity, which is impossible.

This passage builds on the previous refutation by presenting a more rigorous geometric argument. The author uses the relationship between diameters, semicircles, and arcs to show that if an infinite number of possible orbits were to exist, they would have to be actual—a contradiction. Understanding this reinforces the central claim that actual infinity is impossible in creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the geometric terminology: قطر, نصف الدائرة, قوس, مدار.
2
Follow the logical steps
Identify each claim the author makes: the setup about magnitudes, the agreement about circles differing in essence, the assignment of arcs, the uniqueness of positions, and the conclusion about actual infinity.
The argument moves from geometry to a broad metaphysical conclusion.
3
Reflect on the proof
Why does the author call this a 'decisive proof' (برهان قاطع)? Consider how it ties together premises that are accepted by the opponents.
The proof relies on the principle that potential infinity cannot become actual—a key kalam doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نقول : إنا نزيده تأكيداً . فنقول : المقدار الذي يحيط به القطر مع نصف الدائرة ، قابل لقسي مختلفة غير متناهية . والقوم ساعدوا على أن الدوائر المختلفة بالصغر والكبر، مختلفة بالنوعية والماهية . ومعلوم أن كل مدار يقبل قوساً مخصوصاً، فإنه هذه القي، التي لا نهاية لها . وثبت : أن لكل واحد منها موضعا معينا ، يمتنع حصوله في غيره ، ويجب حصوله فيه فحينئذ قد ثبت : أن كل واحد من تلك المدارات مختص بخاصية معينة واجبة الثبوت فيه ، وممتنعة الثبوت في غيره . فحينئذ يلزم حصول التغاير بالفصل بين تلك المدارات . فلو كانت تلك المدارات غير متناهية بالقوة ، لوجب كونها حاصلة بالفعل . وهذا محال [ فذاك محال ] وعلى هذا التقدير فهذا الكلام يصير برهاناً قاطعاً .
Then we say: We reinforce it further. We say: The magnitude enclosed by the diameter with the semicircle is receptive to different arcs without limit. And the people (scholars) agree that circles differing in size differ in type and essence. And it is known that every orbit accepts a specific arc, so these arcs, which have no end. And it is established that each of them has a specific position, impossible to occur in another, and necessary to occur in it. So then it is established that each of those orbits is distinguished by a specific property, necessary of existence in it, and impossible of existence in another. So then it follows that there is differentiation by specific difference among those orbits. So if those orbits were infinite in potential, they would have to be actual. And this is impossible. And on this estimation, this statement becomes a decisive proof.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a reinforcing argument against the possibility of an infinite number of actual entities. The author argues that a diameter with a semicircle can contain infinitely many different arcs. Since circles of different sizes differ in essence, each orbit (circle) has a specific arc. Each such arc must occupy a unique position. Therefore, each orbit has a unique property. If these orbits were infinite in potential, they would have to exist actually—but an actual infinite is deemed impossible. Thus the argument is presented as a decisive proof (burhān qāṭi').

نصف الدائرة

غير متناهية
بالقوة
بالفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This argument is purely about geometry, not theology.
Correction: The geometric claims serve as a premise for a theological conclusion about the impossibility of actual infinity, a core kalam doctrine.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, what would happen if the orbits were infinite in potential?
A) They would remain potential.
B) They would have to be actual.
C) They would be different in essence.
D) They would have the same properties.

Key Takeaway
The geometric argument using diameters and semicircles demonstrates that potential infinity of distinct orbits would necessitate actual infinity, which is considered impossible, thereby reinforcing the refutation of actual infinity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If an actual infinite is impossible, what does that mean for your own life? Are you living as though the present moment is the only one that exists, or do you assume an endless chain of causes?
?
This argument uses geometry to prove a theological truth. Are you willing to let intellectual reasoning shape your certainty about the unseen, even when it challenges comfortable assumptions?
?
The passage insists that distinct properties are actual, not merely potential. Where in your faith do you treat something as merely potential when it should be actual—like gratitude, repentance, or reliance on God?

Third Proof: Euclid's Parallel Postulate
Uses Euclid's postulate to argue against infinite divisibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Euclid's parallel postulate is used in kalam to argue against infinite divisibility.

Core Idea
Euclid's postulate refutes infinite divisibility.

This lesson presents the third proof against infinite divisibility, based on a well-known geometric principle. The author cites Euclid's parallel postulate and then shows that accepting infinite divisibility would contradict this postulate. By following this dialectical reasoning, you will see how kalam engages with mathematics to defend its theological positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to understand Euclid's postulate and the argument that follows.
Notice the conditional structure: 'If ... then ...'
2
Identify Euclid's postulate
Find the statement attributed to Euclid: when a line falls on two straight lines making interior angles less than two right angles, the lines meet on that side.
Geometers agree on this postulate, so it serves as a shared premise.
3
Understand the conditional argument
The author argues that if magnitudes were infinitely divisible, the postulate would be false. Why? Because lines could approach each other forever without meeting, violating the postulate.
This shows the contradiction between infinite divisibility and a accepted geometric truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة : إن و أقليدس ، ذكر في مصادرة المقالة الأولى : « إن كل حطين مستقيمين ، وقع عليها خط آخر ، فتصير الزاويتين اللتين من جهة واحدة ، أقل من قائمتين . فإنهما يلتقيان في تلك الجهة ، فهذا حكم ذكره اقليدس ، واتفق المهندسون على صحته . ونحن نقول : لو كانت المقادير قابلة للقسمة إلى غير النهاية ، لما كان هذا الحكم حقاً . لأن هذين الخطين كلما از دادا امتداداً : از دادا قرباً. لكن تزايد القرب من لا يوجب وصول أحدهما إلى الآخر ، مع القول بكون المقدار قابلا للقسمة إلى غير النهاية . فإن مع القول بهذا المذهب، لا يمتنع وجود مقدارين يتقاربان أبدأ ولا يلتقيان.
The third proof: That Euclid mentioned in the postulate of the first article: 'Whenever two straight lines are intersected by another line, the two angles on one side become less than two right angles, then they meet on that side.' This is a statement mentioned by Euclid, and the engineers (geometers) agreed on its validity. And we say: If magnitudes were divisible to infinity, this statement would not be true. Because these two lines, whenever they increase in extension, increase in proximity. But increasing proximity does not require one to reach the other, given the claim that magnitude is divisible to infinity. For with this doctrine, it is not impossible for two magnitudes to approach forever and never meet.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof against infinite divisibility, based on Euclid's parallel postulate. The author quotes Euclid's postulate: if a line falls on two straight lines making interior angles on one side less than two right angles, the lines meet on that side. Euclidean geometers agree on this. The author then argues: if magnitudes were infinitely divisible, this postulate would be false. Because two lines can increase in proximity indefinitely without ever meeting, as infinite divisibility allows them to approach forever but never touch. Thus, the validity of the postulate refutes infinite divisibility.

Key Terms
أقليدس
المقالة الأولى
مسلمة
مقادير
قسمة إلى غير النهاية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some readers might think the author is criticizing Euclidean geometry or rejecting Euclid's postulate.
Correction: The author uses Euclid's postulate as a shared premise that is widely accepted. The argument is directed against the philosophical claim of infinite divisibility, not against geometry.

Checkpoint
How does the author use Euclid's postulate to argue against infinite divisibility?
A) By showing that infinite divisibility contradicts the postulate that lines meet when interior angles are less than two right angles.
B) By proving that Euclid's postulate is false.
C) By showing that infinite divisibility makes all lines parallel.
D) By demonstrating that Euclid did not believe in infinite divisibility.

Key Takeaway
Euclid's parallel postulate, if accepted, implies that infinite divisibility is false because two lines approaching forever without meeting would contradict the postulate.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The argument shows that infinite divisibility leads to a contradiction with a known truth. Are there contradictions in your own beliefs that you have ignored because they are uncomfortable to resolve? What step will you take to address one such contradiction this week?
?
The proof builds on accepted premises to reach a conclusion. Reflect on the foundations of your most deeply held beliefs: Are they built on premises that you have truly examined, or have you accepted them uncritically? Commit to questioning one such premise today.

Apollonius's Asymptotes as a Supporting Proof
Cites Apollonius's Conics to show lines that approach forever without meeting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Apollonius's demonstration of asymptotic curves supports the argument that infinite approach does not necessitate meeting.

Core Idea
Asymptotes prove that going closer forever does not force a meeting.

This lesson introduces the first supporting proof for the earlier claim about converging lines. The author calls upon the ancient geometer Apollonius, whose work on conic sections revealed curves that eternally approach without intersecting. This geometric fact becomes a powerful analogy for the logical point about infinite divisibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text attentively. Notice that it begins by announcing a proof, then names Apollonius, and then draws a conclusion.
The phrase 'وذلك يدل' signals the logical inference.
2
Identify the two key parts
First, Apollonius demonstrated the existence of two lines that forever approach but never meet. Second, this shows that increasing proximity without limit does not force intersection.
Separate the factual observation from the logical implication.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this geometric example supports the broader argument about infinity: just because something gets closer and closer does not mean it will ever reach the target.
This is a counterexample to the assumption that continual approach implies eventual meeting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والذي يدل على صحة ما ذكرناه . وجوه : الأول : إن «أبلونيوس ) بين في كتاب ( المخروطـات ، وجود خطين يتقاربان أبداً ولا يلتقيان . وذلك يدل على أن التزايد في القرب إلى غير النهاية ، لا يوجب حصول الالتقاء .
And what indicates the validity of what we mentioned: Aspects. First: That Apollonius demonstrated in the book of Conics the existence of two lines that approach forever and never meet. And that indicates that increase in proximity to infinity does not necessitate the occurrence of meeting.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is the first of four supporting proofs. The author cites Apollonius of Perga's work 'Conics', which demonstrated the existence of asymptotic lines—lines that approach each other indefinitely but never intersect. This example shows that infinite approach does not require meeting, thus supporting the earlier argument that under infinite divisibility, converging lines might never meet, contrary to Euclid's postulate. The author uses this as empirical evidence from geometry.

Key Terms

المخروطات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Apollonius's asymptotes are a counterexample to Euclid's parallel postulate.
Correction: Asymptotes are curves, not straight lines, so they do not conflict with Euclidean geometry about parallel lines.

Checkpoint

A) That all lines eventually meet.
B) That two lines can approach each other forever without meeting.
C) That infinite divisibility is impossible.
D) That Euclid's postulate is false.

Key Takeaway
Infinite proximity does not guarantee meeting, as shown by Apollonius's asymptotic curves.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You often assume that if you get closer to a goal, you must eventually reach it. But this lesson shows that infinite approach does not guarantee meeting. In your spiritual journey, do you assume that simply getting closer to Allah over time ensures you will meet Him? What if your approach is asymptotic—ever closer but never actually turning to Him? Will you settle for approximation or seek true meeting?
?
The lines in the proof approach but never meet. Have you ever convinced yourself that you are 'close enough' to righteousness, never actually meeting the standard? How does that asymptotic excuse keep you from true repentance? What one step today would break the pattern of mere approach?
?
Apollonius's discovery was used to prove a theological point. Are you willing to let mathematical truths challenge your comfortable assumptions about God? Or do you dismiss such proofs as irrelevant? What does your reluctance say about your faith?

Square Division and Infinite Approach
Uses division of a square to show lines approach but never meet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how geometric infinite divisibility demonstrates lines that approach forever without meeting, supporting the denial of the indivisible atom.

Core Idea
Infinite division of a square proves lines can approach forever without touching.

This proof uses a simple geometric thought experiment to show that if a surface can be divided infinitely, then a dividing line can approach one side indefinitely without ever reaching it. The argument relies on the denial of indivisible atoms, which is a key premise in the discussion of atomism. As we examine the reasoning, we'll see how it establishes the existence of pairs of lines that eternally approach but never meet.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author starts by stating a premise about geometry and the indivisible atom.
2
Understand the premise
The proof begins by asserting that geometry is based on the denial of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). This means infinite divisibility is assumed.
This premise is crucial for the entire argument.
3
Visualize the bisection
Imagine a square with a fixed distance between two opposite sides. When you bisect the square, the dividing line is closer to one side than the original. Each subsequent bisection brings the dividing line even closer.
Draw a simple diagram to help visualize.
4
Follow the infinite chain
Since the surface can be bisected infinitely many times, the dividing line keeps approaching the side infinitely but never reaches it. If it did reach, the number of divisions would be finite, contradicting infinite divisibility.
This is the core logical step.
5
Grasp the conclusion
The argument concludes that there exist two lines (the dividing line and the side) that approach each other forever without meeting. This supports the denial of the indivisible atom.
This conclusion is used as a supporting proof in the broader context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : إن علم الهندسة مبني على نفي الجوهر الفرد . إذا ثبت هذا ، فلنفرض سطحاً مربعاً . بين أحد الضلعين والآخر بعد معين . فإذا نصفنا ذلك السطح ، صار هذا الخط الذي أوجب التنصيف ، أقرب إلى أحد الطرفين . فإذا نصفنا ذلك النصف، صار هذا الخط الثاني، أقرب . ثم لما كان ذلك السطح يقبل التنصيف إلى غير النهاية ، فحينئذ يكون الخط القاسم ، لا يزال يقرب من ذلك الطرف إلى غير النهاية . والبتة لا يصل إليه . إذ لو وصل إليه . لكان احتمال قبول ذلك السطح للقسمة متناهياً . وقد فرضناه غير متناه . فثبت : وجود خطين يتقاربان أبدا ولا يلتقيان .
Second: That the science of geometry is based on the denial of the indivisible atom. If this is established, then let us suppose a square surface. Between one side and the other is a certain distance. So if we bisect that surface, this line that necessitated the bisection becomes closer to one of the ends. Then if we bisect that half, this second line becomes closer. Then since that surface accepts bisection to infinity, then the dividing line keeps approaching that end to infinity, and never reaches it. For if it reached it, then the possibility of that surface accepting division would be finite, but we have assumed it infinite. So it is established that there exist two lines that approach forever and never meet.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is the second supporting proof. It begins by asserting that geometry is based on the denial of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). The author then constructs a thought experiment: take a square surface with a fixed distance between two opposite sides. By repeatedly bisecting the square, each dividing line gets closer to one side. Since the square can be bisected infinitely many times, the dividing lines approach the side infinitely but never reach it. If it did reach, the square would have only finitely many divisions, contradicting the assumption of infinite divisibility. Hence, the existence of lines that approach without meeting is established, supporting the earlier argument.

Key Terms
جوهر فرد
سطح مربع
تنصيف
غير متناه
خط قاسم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking this proof is about actual physical squares that can be divided infinitely in reality.
Correction: It is a logical thought experiment assuming infinite divisibility to prove the existence of non-meeting converging lines, not a claim about physical reality.

Checkpoint
What assumption does the square division example rely on?
A) That atoms exist.
B) That geometry is based on the denial of the indivisible atom.
C) That the square has finite area.
D) That division stops at some point.

Key Takeaway
Through infinite divisibility, geometry shows that two lines can approach each other forever but never meet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that you can rationally accept something your senses cannot directly see—like infinite approach without meeting. In what area of your faith do you struggle to accept a truth because you cannot perceive it? Will you commit to basing your certainty on clear rational proofs rather than on what you feel or see?
?
If the finite world contains infinite potential divisions, how much more infinite must the Creator be? Does this reflection challenge your tendency to limit Allah in your mind? What one thought about Allah's infinity will you carry into your next prayer?

Parallel Lines and Infinite Approach
Demonstrates with parallel lines on a surface that lines approach indefinitely without meeting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the geometric reasoning of parallel lines and complements demonstrates the possibility of infinite approach without meeting.

Core Idea
Two lines can approach each other forever without ever meeting.

This lesson continues the series of supporting proofs for a key theological point. The author uses a geometric construction involving two lines parallel to the sides of a surface to show that one line can approach the other indefinitely, yet never reach it. This parallels the idea of an infinite temporal series that approaches a limit without crossing it.

Guided Path
1
Understand the geometric setup
Start by grasping the initial premise: the two complements must be equal (from a previous article). Then note the construction: two lines parallel to the length and width of a surface.
The 'complements' likely refer to the two rectangles formed by the parallels.
2
Follow the relationship between distances
Observe that as the line parallel to the width moves farther from the width line, the line parallel to the length moves closer to the length line.
This inverse relationship is key to the argument.
3
Recognize the infinite degrees
Since the width-parallel line can be placed at an infinite number of distances, the length-parallel line has an infinite number of closeness degrees.
The argument relies on the unbounded nature of distance.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The length-parallel line approaches the length line infinitely but never reaches it; otherwise they would coincide impossibly.
This establishes that infinite approach without meeting is possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : إنه ثبت في المقالة الأولى : أن المتهمين يجب كونهما متساويين . إذا عرفت هذا ، فنقول : هذان المتممان ، إنما يحدثان بسبب حصول خطين : أحدهما يوازي طول السطح، والثاني يوازي عرضه . ثم كلما كان الخط الموازي للعرض أبعد ، عن الخط العرضي ، صار الخط الموازي للطول ، أقرب إلى الخط الطولي . ولما كان لا نهاية لمراتب بعد الخط الموازي للعرض ، وجب أن يكون لا نهاية لمراتب قرب الخط الموازي للطول . والبتة لا يصل إليه . وإلا لصار ذلك الخط الطولي مساوياً لذلك السطح . وهو محال . فثبت : أن الخط الموازي للطول يقرب من الطول أبداً . والبتة لا يصل إليه . ولا يلقاه .
Third: It is established in the first article that the two complements must be equal. If you know this, then we say: These two complements occur only due to the presence of two lines: one parallel to the length of the surface, and the second parallel to its width. Then whenever the line parallel to the width is farther from the width line, the line parallel to the length becomes closer to the length line. And since there is no limit to the degrees of distance of the line parallel to the width, it follows that there is no limit to the degrees of closeness of the line parallel to the length. And it never reaches it. Otherwise, that length line would become equal to that surface, which is impossible. So it is established that the line parallel to the length approaches the length forever, and never reaches it, and does not meet it.
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is the third supporting proof. It references a proposition from the first article (likely Euclidean geometry) that the two complements (the rectangles formed by parallels) are equal. The author constructs a rectangle with a line parallel to the length and another parallel to the width. As the line parallel to the width moves farther away from the width line, the line parallel to the length moves closer to the length line. Since the distance of the width-parallel line can increase infinitely, the closeness of the length-parallel line can also increase infinitely, but it never reaches the length line. If it did, the length line would equal the entire surface, which is impossible. Thus, the proof shows again that two lines can approach each other indefinitely without meeting.

Key Terms
المتممان
متوازي
خط طولي
خط عرضي
مراتب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If two lines approach each other infinitely, they must eventually meet.
Correction: The proof shows that infinite approach can occur without meeting, as the length line never becomes equal to the entire surface.

Checkpoint
What is the conclusion of the third supporting proof?
A) Lines parallel to the length and width always meet.
B) A line parallel to the length can approach the length infinitely without reaching it.
C) All lines in a rectangle are parallel.
D) The complements are never equal.

Key Takeaway
This proof establishes that infinite approach without meeting is geometrically possible, supporting arguments about infinite series in theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your spiritual journey, are you content with drawing closer to Allah without ever fully comprehending His essence, or do you feel frustrated by the infinite gap? How does this geometric truth about infinite approach without meeting change your perspective?
?
Consider a goal you have been pursuing for years that remains out of reach. Does this proof encourage you to continue the approach, or does it feel like futility? What does the lesson say about the value of drawing nearer even without reaching?
?
The length line cannot equal the surface without contradiction. Is there an area in your life where you are demanding a 'meeting'—an immediate result or complete understanding—when you should instead be content with infinite approach? What would it mean to trust the process of drawing closer?

The First Proof: Why Indivisible Parts Cannot Touch
First proof: impossibility of atom contact.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first kalam proof that atoms cannot be in contact, and why this leads to the impossibility of bodies being composed of indivisible parts.

Core Idea
If atoms could touch, they would have to do so wholly or partially—both lead to absurdities.

This passage introduces the first of five proofs in a chapter on contact. The author aims to demonstrate that indivisible atoms cannot physically touch each other. Through a logical dichotomy, he shows that both total and partial contact are impossible, thereby undermining the atomist theory of body composition.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the author starts with the conclusion, then provides a logical division (either total contact or not total).
The word 'المخرعة' may be a typo; the context is proofs about contact.
2
Understand the dichotomy
The author says if atoms touch, it must be either total contact (the whole of one touches the whole of the other) or partial contact. He then argues both are impossible.
This is a standard kalam argument by contradiction.
3
Analyze the first argument against total contact
Suppose two atoms touch wholly. Ask: does the combined volume increase? If yes, they are not wholly touching; if no, no body formation. Both options are contradictory.
This shows that total contact leads to paradox.
4
Consider the second (incomplete) argument
The second argument discusses interpenetration. If atoms completely interpenetrate, they become indistinguishable, so no multiple parts exist.
The passage cuts off here, but the point is clear.
5
Reflect on the overall proof
The proof refutes atomism by showing contact between indivisible parts is incoherent. Thus bodies cannot be made of atoms.
This is a key argument in Islamic kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي خمسة :
الفصل الأول
في
الدلائل المخرعة على المماسة
البرهان الأول : إن الأجزاء التي لا تتجزا ، يمتنع أن تكون متلاقية . وإذا كان كذلك ، امتنع حصول الأجسام عنها. إنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع كونها متلاقية . لأنها لو تلاقت ، لكانت إما أن تكون متلاقية بالكلية ، أو لا بالكلية . والقسمان باطلان ، فوجب القول بأنه يمتنع كونها متلاقية
إنما قلنا : إنه يمتنع كونها متلاقية بالكلية . لوجوه :
الأول : إنا إذا فرضنا جوهراً واحداً اتصل به جوهر ثاني فهل صار حجم مجموع الجزئين ، أزيد من حجم الجزء الواحد ، أو ما حصلت هذه الزيادة ؟ فإن كان الأول ، فحينئذ يكون كل واحد منها خارجاً عن ذات الآخر ، وغير نافذ فيه . وعلى هذا التقدير، فلم تصر كلية أحدهما ملاقية لكلية الآخر . وإن كان الثاني ، فحينئذ يكون مجموع الجزئين مساوياً في الحجم للجزء الواحد فحينئذ لو ضممنا إليه ثالثاً ورابعاً ، وجب أن لا تحصل الزيادة في الحجم. وحينئذ لا تكون هذه المقادير والأحجام ، متولدة عن تأليف هذه الأجزاء ، وقد فرضنا : أن الأمر كذلك . هذا خلف .
الثاني : إن هذه الأجزاء إذا تداخلت ونفذ بعضها في بعض . فنقول : إنه لم يحصل الامتياز بينها في أمر من الأمور البتة . فوجب صيرورتها شيئاً
And they are five:
The first chapter
On
the proofs [المخرعة؟] concerning contact.
The first proof: That the indivisible parts cannot be in contact. And if that is so, then the formation of bodies from them is impossible. We say: Their being in contact is impossible. Because if they were in contact, they would either be in contact entirely, or not entirely. Both divisions are false, so it is necessary to say that their being in contact is impossible.
We say: Their being entirely in contact is impossible, for reasons:
First: If we suppose one atom (جوهر) joined by a second atom, then does the volume of the sum of the two parts become greater than the volume of the single part, or does this increase not occur? If the first, then each one would be outside the essence of the other and not penetrating into it. On this assumption, the whole of one does not contact the whole of the other. If the second, then the sum of the two parts would be equal in volume to the single part; then if we added a third and a fourth to it, no increase in volume would necessarily occur. Then these magnitudes and volumes would not be generated from the composition of these parts, while we have assumed that it is so. This is a contradiction.
Second: If these parts interpenetrate and some penetrate others, we say: No distinction between them occurs in any matter at all. So they must become a single thing.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is the first proof of a chapter on proofs concerning contact (المماسة). The author begins by stating the proof's conclusion: indivisible parts (atoms) cannot be in contact with each other, and therefore bodies cannot be formed from them. He then explains the reasoning: if atoms could touch, they would have to do so either wholly or partially. Both possibilities are shown to be absurd.

The author first argues against total contact. He supposes two atoms (جوهران) coming together. He asks whether the combined volume increases or not. If it increases, then each atom remains outside the other, so they are not wholly in contact—only partially. If it does not increase, then the combined volume equals that of a single atom, implying that adding more atoms would never increase volume, contradicting the observed fact that bodies have varying sizes. This is a reductio ad absurdum.

The second argument (though the text appears cut off) considers interpenetration: if atoms completely merge without distinction, they become one single thing, not multiple parts. Thus contact is impossible. The proof follows a standard kalam dialectical pattern, refuting the atomist view that bodies are composed of indivisible parts.

Key Terms
الجزء الذي لا يتجزأ
المماسة
الجوهر
الكلية
التداخل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Atoms cannot touch because they are too small or have no size.
Correction: The proof does not rely on size but on logical consequences of contact: total contact leads to paradoxes with volume and interpenetration.

Checkpoint
In the first proof, what is the first reason given for rejecting total contact between two atoms?
A) If volume increases, they are not wholly in contact.
B) Atoms are too small to touch.
C) The atoms would merge into one.
D) The author assumes atoms are indivisible.

Key Takeaway
The first proof establishes that atoms cannot be in contact, undermining the atomist theory that bodies are composed of indivisible parts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof uses logical contradiction to show that atoms cannot touch. Where in your own life have you held onto a belief that, when carefully examined, leads to contradiction? Will you have the courage to abandon that belief for the sake of truth?

The proof demonstrates that our physical world cannot be explained by simple parts just coming together. How does this deepen your reliance on the Creator as the true cause of all existence? Will you let this truth transform your daily awareness of God's power?
?
If atoms cannot even touch, then the very existence of bodies is a miracle. How should this affect your gratitude for the simple fact that you can move, speak, and interact with the world? What one action will you take today to acknowledge this dependence?

Proof that the Right and Left Sides of a Body Are Not Distinct
Concludes that two sides of a simple body cannot be distinct.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the right and left sides of a simple body cannot be distinct, based on the impossibility of two contradictories being true of the same subject.

Core Idea
Two contradictories cannot be true of the same simple substance.

Here the author presents a concise logical argument that the right and left sides of a simple body must be identical, not distinct. If they were distinct, contradictory properties would apply to the same object, which is rationally impossible. Let's examine the reasoning closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the flow of the argument.
2
Identify the contradictory predicates
Note what is said about the right side and the left side: they have opposite rulings. The right side does not correspond to the left, and the left side has the opposite.
3
Understand the impossibility
If the two sides were distinct, then the same body would have two contradictory properties at once. This is impossible (muḥāl) because two contradictories cannot be true of one thing.
This is a fundamental principle of logic.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Therefore, the two sides cannot be distinct; they are identical in the simple body.
The author says 'this is the summary of the discourse' to conclude.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على اليمين ، ولا يحاذي ما على اليسار . وجانب اليسار منه محكوم عليه بضد ذلك . فلو كان الجانب الأيمن منه ، غير الجانب الأيسر ، لزم أن يصدق النقيضان على الشيء الواحد . وإنه محال . فهذا جملة الكلام في تقرير هذا الوجه
what is on the right, and it does not correspond to what is on the left. And the left side of it is ruled by the opposite of that. So if the right side of it were other than the left side, it would necessarily follow that two contradictories are true of one thing. And that is impossible. This is the summary of the discourse in establishing this aspect.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a brief proof that the right and left sides of a simple body cannot be distinct. It begins by stating that what is on the right does not correspond to what is on the left, and the left side is ruled by the opposite. If the two sides were different, then two contradictory predicates would apply to the same subject, which is impossible. The author concludes that this summary establishes the point.

Key Terms

الشيء الواحد
محال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the right and left sides of a body are physically or spatially distinct parts of the body.
Correction: The argument is about the logical impossibility of two contradictory properties applying to a simple (undivided) substance. It does not deny that we can conceive of right and left as relational aspects, but they cannot be two distinct entities in the body itself.

Checkpoint

A) They are distinct.
B) They cannot be distinct.
C) They are both the same.
D) They are opposites.

Key Takeaway
The right and left sides of a simple body cannot be distinct because their distinctness would entail a logical contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson uses the impossibility of contradictory attributes in a simple substance. Name one area where your actions contradict your professed beliefs, and commit to aligning them from today.
?
The proof argues that distinctness leads to logical impossibility. Consider your own character: do you ever claim virtues (like patience or honesty) while acting oppositely? That too is a form of contradiction. What specific contradiction in your character will you work to remove, and how will you hold yourself accountable this week?

The Motion Argument Against Indivisible Parts
Thought experiment proving indivisible parts must divide.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a thought experiment about motion in a void proves that indivisible parts must necessarily divide.

Core Idea
A void between parts forces contradictory divisions.

Sanusi presents a clever thought experiment to expose a contradiction in atomism. He assumes a line of three parts with a void between two end parts. When those parts move toward each other, they must each contact part of the middle piece, forcing it to divide. This shows that indivisible parts cannot exist under the laws of motion.

Guided Path
1
Understand the setup
A line of three equal parts. Two parts at the ends with a void (equal to one part) between them. The middle part is a separate line below? Actually, the argument says 'خطاً مركباً من ثلاثة أجزاء' and then 'جزئين على طرفيه' — so the line has three parts, and we place two parts at its ends (maybe above? The commentary says 'two smaller parts' but the text says 'جزئين على طرفيه' — likely the same line? The translation says 'two parts at its two ends' but then 'intermediate part of the lower line' so there are two lines: an upper line with two parts, and a lower line with three parts? The Arabic is ambiguous but the argument is standard. We'll follow the provided translation. The key is the setup: a line of three parts (lower line) and two parts (upper line) at the ends with a void between them equal to one part.
Read the passage carefully to see the full setup.
2
Identify the conditions for motion
Each end part is capable of motion (قابل للحركة) and the obstacle (مانع) is absent because the void is empty. Therefore motion is possible.
The argument relies on the principle: if a thing is capable and no obstacle, motion is necessary (or possible).
3
Conclude the necessary division
When both end parts move together, each must meet half of the intermediate part of the lower line. This forces the intermediate part to divide, and consequently all five parts divide.
The conclusion contradicts the assumption of indivisibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثانية : أن نقول : إذا فرضنا خطاً مركباً من ثلاثة أجزاء ، وفرضنا جزئين على طرفيه ، بحيث بقي بينهما خلاء ، بمقدار الجزء الواحد فنقول : كل واحد من هذين الجزئين الموضوعين على الطرفين ، قابل للحركة . والمانع من الحركة : مفقود لأنا فرضنا ذلك المتوسط خالياً عن جميع العوائق وإذا كان الشيء قابلاً للحركة ، وكان المانع من الحركة مفقوداً ، وجب أن تكون الحركة ممكنة . فإذا تحرك الجزءان ، الموضوعان على الطرفين معاً ، وجب أن يلقى كل واحد منهما نصف الجزء المتوسط من الخط الأسفل . بل نقول : إن كل واحد من هذين الجزءين الفوقانيين ، يقع على متصل جزءين من الخط الأسفل . وحينئذ يلزم انقسام الأجزاء الخمسة جميعاً .
The second argument: We say: If we assume a line composed of three parts, and we assume two parts at its two ends, such that between them remains a void equal to one part, then we say: Each of these two parts placed at the ends is capable of motion. And the obstacle to motion is absent because we have assumed that intermediate [space] empty of all impediments. And if something is capable of motion, and the obstacle to motion is absent, motion must be possible. So if the two parts placed at the ends move together, each of them must meet half of the intermediate part of the lower line. Rather we say: Each of these two upper parts falls onto two contiguous parts of the lower line. Then the division of all five parts necessarily follows.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage presents the second argument in a series concerning indivisible parts. The author imagines a line of three equal parts, with a void also of one part's width between them. Two smaller parts are placed at the ends. Since nothing blocks them, they can move toward each other. When they do, each would land on half of the middle part, forcing it to divide. The conclusion is that all five parts (the three original plus the two moving) must divide, which contradicts the assumption of indivisible atoms.

Key Terms

خلاء
حركة
مانع
انقسام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is about physical bodies and real motion in void space.
Correction: The argument is a logical thought experiment to show that the hypothesis of indivisible atoms leads to a contradiction, not a description of actual physical motion.

Checkpoint
According to the second argument, what must happen when the two end parts move together?
A) They stop in the void.
B) They meet each other.
C) They force division of the intermediate part.
D) They bounce back.

Key Takeaway
The second argument uses a thought experiment to prove that indivisible parts cannot move without causing division, contradicting their assumed indivisibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Objection to the Second Argument: Circularity
Opponent's objection exposing circularity in the second argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the opponent exposes circular reasoning in the second argument by distinguishing between obstacles and conditions for possibility.

Core Idea
Possibility requires conditions, not just absence of obstacles – circularity cannot stand.

The second argument claimed that the two end parts can move because they are capable and obstacles are absent. But an opponent raises a deeper point: possibility requires not only the absence of obstacles but also the presence of conditions. Here we examine that objection and the charge of circularity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice that the opponent first quotes the original argument and then responds.
The opponent says 'we do not grant' (لا نسلم), a typical objection marker.
2
Identify the key concepts: condition vs. obstacle
The opponent argues that in assessing possibility, both absence of obstacles (mani') and presence of conditions (shart) are necessary. Find where these terms appear in the passage.
The condition is the division of the intermediate part.
3
Trace the circularity
The opponent shows that to prove motion, one must prove division; but division is supposed to follow from motion. This creates a vicious circle (dawr). Write down the logical steps that lead to circularity.
The passage ends with 'لزم الدور' (circularity follows).
4
Evaluate the force of the objection
Consider whether the objection successfully refutes the second argument. Does it show that the argument is invalid, or only that it is incomplete? Discuss with a partner if possible.
The objection attacks the reasoning, not the conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولقائل أن يقول : لا نسلم أنه يمكن حصول حركة الجزءين الموضوعين على الطرفين معا أما قوله : ( إن كل واحد منهما قابل للحركة . والحيز المتوسط فارغ ، والمانع مفقود ، فوجب صحة الحركة على كل واحد منهما ) ، فنقول : هب أن كل واحد منهما قابل للحركة، وأن المانع مفقود . فلم قلتم : إن هذا القدر ، يقتضي إمكان تلك الحركة ؟ وبيانه : أن الشيء كما يعتبر في إمكانه تحقق إمكانه في ذاته ، وانتفاء موانعه . فكذلك يعتبر في تحقق إمكانه حصول شرائطه . ولا شك أن حركة ذينك الجزئين مشروط بانقسام ذلك الجزء المتوسط من الخط الأسفل ، وبتقدير أن لا يكون ذلك الجزء منقسماً ، كان شرط إمكان حركة الجزءين الموضوعين على الطرفين فائناً . وإذا كان الشرط فائناً ، وإذا كان المشروط ممتنعاً . فثبت : أن القطع بإمكان حركة ذينك الجزءين إنما يمكن عند القطع بانقسام ذلك الجزء المتوسط. فلو أثبتنا كون الجزء المتوسط منقسماً ، يكون ذينك الجزءين قابلين للحركة . لزم الدور . وهو باطل
And someone may say: We do not grant that motion of the two parts placed at the ends can occur together. As for his statement: 'Each of them is capable of motion, and the intermediate space is empty, and the obstacle is absent, so the validity of motion for each of them is necessary,' we say: Grant that each of them is capable of motion and that the obstacle is absent. But why do you say that this much necessitates the possibility of that motion? Its explanation: A thing, as consideration is given in its possibility to the realization of its possibility in itself and the negation of its obstacles, likewise consideration is given in the realization of its possibility to the attainment of its conditions. And there is no doubt that the motion of those two parts is conditioned by the division of that intermediate part of the lower line. And assuming that that part is not divided, the condition for the possibility of motion of the two parts placed at the ends would be non-existent. And when the condition is non-existent, the conditioned is impossible. So it is established that certainty of the possibility of motion of those two parts is only possible upon certainty of the division of that intermediate part. So if we prove that the intermediate part is divided, then those two parts are capable of motion. That leads to circularity, which is invalid.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage presents an objection from an opponent. The opponent first quotes the original argument's claim that each end part is movable and the void provides no obstacle. Then the opponent responds: even if we grant that, the possibility of motion requires not only absence of obstacles but also presence of conditions. The motion here requires that the intermediate part be divisible. Without that division, motion is impossible. To prove motion one must first prove division, but division is supposed to follow from motion. This is circular and invalid. The objection thus refutes the second argument by showing it presupposes what it tries to prove.

Key Terms
شرط
مانع
دور
مشروط
إمكان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection denies that motion can occur.
Correction: The objection does not deny motion; it shows that the argument's reasoning is logically circular and therefore invalid.

Checkpoint
What logical fallacy does the objection claim the second argument commits?
A) Ad hominem
B) Circular reasoning
C) False dilemma
D) Straw man

Key Takeaway
The objection shows that the second argument's reasoning is invalid because it presupposes what it tries to prove, creating a vicious circle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you argue for something in your own life, do you check whether you are assuming what you want to prove? How might circular reasoning be hiding in your daily decisions or beliefs?

The opponent in this passage distinguishes between absence of obstacles and presence of conditions. In your relationship with Allah, are you content with simply avoiding sins (absence of obstacles) without actively seeking the conditions for true worship? What condition might you be neglecting?

The Circularity Argument on Middle Part Divisibility
A brief argument showing circularity in proving divisibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how assuming the divisibility of the middle part leads to a vicious circle, and why this invalidates the argument.

Core Idea
Circular reasoning cannot prove atomic divisibility.

This passage presents a concise logical argument against a claim about atomic divisibility. The author shows that if we try to prove the middle part is divisible, we end up in a circularity, making the argument unsound. Let's trace the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the overall argument.
Notice the key terms: الجزء المتوسط (middle part), الانقسام (division), الدور (circularity).
2
Identify the conditional structure
The argument is structured as a conditional: if we prove divisibility, then motion follows, which leads to circularity.
The word فلو (if) introduces the assumption, and لزم (follows) introduces the consequence.
3
Understand the circularity
The author claims that proving divisibility requires motion, but motion itself relies on divisibility, creating a circle. Why is this a problem? Because circular arguments do not provide independent proof.
In logic, a vicious circle (دور) is a fallacy where the conclusion is assumed in the premise.
4
Conclude the argument's validity
The author concludes that the argument is false (باطل) because it leads to circularity. This means the premise that the middle part is divisible cannot be proven in this way.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القطع بانقسام ذلك الجزء المتوسط. فلو أثبتنا كون الجزء المتوسط منقسماً ، يكون ذينك الجزءين قابلين للحركة . لزم الدور . وهو باطل
The certainty of division of that middle part. For if we prove that the middle part is divisible, then those two parts are capable of motion. Circularity would follow, and it is false.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage presents a short argument against the divisibility of the middle part of a line composed of atoms. It states that if we assume the middle part is divisible, then the two resulting parts would be movable, but that leads to a vicious circle (dawr) which is unacceptable. The reasoning is that the divisibility itself is what is in question, and using it to prove motion would be circular. The author asserts this is false, thus rejecting the premise that the middle part is divisible.

Key Terms
القطع
الجزء المتوسط
الانقسام
الحركة
الدور
باطل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the argument is about physical impossibility of motion or a contradiction in the nature of atoms.
Correction: The argument is purely logical: it shows that the proof of divisibility leads to circular reasoning, not that motion or divisibility is impossible in itself.

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude about proving the divisibility of the middle part?
A) It is possible and leads to valid motion.
B) It leads to a logical circularity and is therefore false.
C) It is necessary for the existence of atoms.
D) It depends on the definition of motion.

Key Takeaway
The divisibility of the middle part cannot be proven without falling into circular reasoning, making the argument invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used circular reasoning to justify a belief without realizing it? How can you guard against this in your own thinking?
?
When you encounter an argument that seems to rely on its own conclusion, do you have the courage to reject it as invalid, even if it aligns with what you want to believe?
?
Reflect on a time when you were convinced by an argument that later turned out to be circular. How did you feel when you discovered the fallacy? How can you train yourself to spot circularity in arguments about faith?

First Proof of Possibility: The Triangle and Composite Line
Author constructs a geometric argument to show that an indivisible part can contact two others, proving possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author constructs a geometric argument to prove that an indivisible part can contact two others, thereby establishing the possibility that undermines an objection.

Core Idea
A single atom can touch two others—geometry proves it's possible.

This passage tackles a crucial objection against the existence of indivisible parts (atoms). The author uses a simple geometric construction—a triangle and a composite line—to show that it is possible for an indivisible part to be in contact with two others simultaneously. This logical possibility undermines the objection and reinforces the atomic theory.

Guided Path
1
Understand the geometric construction
Read the passage and visualize the configuration: a line composed of three parts placed along one side of a triangle, such that each part touches two parts in a line of four parts.
The triangle is equilateral and the parts are indivisible (atoms).
2
See the generalization
The author states that this can be extended to all higher levels ad infinitum. Notice the phrase 'قس عليه سائر المراتب'—'apply the same to the remaining levels.'
3
Grasp the conclusion
The construction forces the conclusion that an equilateral triangle composed of parts requires each part to contact two others. This shows that such contact is possible, and therefore the objection against the proof of atoms is repelled.
The passage ends by stating the objection is repelled if this is possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصلنا خطاً مركباً من ثلاثة أجزاء، بأحد أضلاع المثلث المذكور ، بحيث يقع كل واحد من تلك الأجزاء على متصل جزءين من الأجزاء ، الحاصلة في هذا الخط المركب من الأجزاء الأربعة . وقس عليه سائر المراتب إلى ما لا نهاية له . وحينئذ يظهر أنه لا يمكن وجود مثلث متساوي الأضلاع من الأجزاء ، إلا ويقع كل واحد منها على متصل جزءين آخرين. وذلك يدل على أن هذا المعنى : ممكن. وإذا كان ممكناً ، فحينئذ يندفع هذا السؤال ، عن ذلك الدليل
We constructed a line composed of three parts, with one of the sides of the aforementioned triangle, such that each one of those parts lies in contact with two parts of the parts occurring in this line composed of four parts. And apply the same to the remaining levels ad infinitum. Then it becomes apparent that it is impossible for an equilateral triangle composed of parts to exist unless each one of them lies in contact with two other parts. And that indicates that this meaning is possible. And if it is possible, then this objection against that proof is repelled.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage presents a geometric proof from possibility. The author explains that by constructing a line composed of three parts (atoms) along one side of a triangle, each part touches two others in a line of four parts. This can be extended to higher orders. The key conclusion is that an equilateral triangle built from indivisible parts requires each part to be in contact with two others. This demonstrates the possibility of a single part contacting two other parts, which refutes an objection against the proof for the existence of indivisible parts. The structure is: (1) Construction of the configuration. (2) Generalization to all levels. (3) Conclusion that the configuration is possible, hence the objection fails.

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The argument does not claim actual existence; it only demonstrates logical possibility, which is sufficient to defeat an objection that claims impossibility.

The Philosophers' Contact Argument and the Leap (Talfra) Response
The philosophers' third argument based on motion and contact, and the leap (talfra) response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' third argument for the possibility of one substance contacting two substances, and the debate among atomists about the concept of 'leap' (talfra).

Core Idea
The contact argument forces a division of atoms, but some atomists accept a 'leap' to avoid it.

This passage presents a key argument from the philosophers that aims to prove that a substance can contact two others simultaneously, leading to a division of the atom. The author then reports a controversy among the proponents of the indivisible atom: some adopt the 'leap' (talfra) to evade the conclusion, while others reject the leap and accept the argument as valid. Let's examine the argument and the response.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get the overall flow of the argument and the subsequent discussion.
The passage contains a thought experiment with a line of four parts.
2
Identify the philosophers' scenario
Understand the setup: a line of four atoms, two parts placed above the ends, moving to the other side, and the necessity of alignment and opposition at the contact of the second and third.
This is the core of the contact argument.
3
Understand the conclusion
The scenario forces division (gisma) of the parts, showing that one substance can contact two.
This is the third proof for the possibility.
4
Examine the leap response
Some atomists accept the leap to avoid the conclusion that alignment requires continuous motion. They argue that if we allow a leap, alignment is not necessary.
The author notes that opponents of the leap consider the proof sound.
5
Reflect on the two positions
Consider the disagreement: leap vs. no leap, and what it implies for the indivisible atom.
This shows internal debate among kalam scholars.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The third aspect in demonstrating that the matter we mentioned is possible: it is that in the third argument of the philosophers it is shown by certain proof that the occurrence of the substance upon the contact of two substances is actual. And if that is so, then this problem is removed. The third argument of the philosophers from the aspects based on contact and meeting: we say: If two composed a line of four parts, and we placed a part above its right end, and placed another part above its left end. Then we assumed that these two parts began movement and reached the end of the line simultaneously. Then each of these two parts passes by the other. And it is impossible for each of them to pass by the other unless alignment and opposition occur between them. And it is impossible for alignment and opposition to occur except upon the contact of the second and the third. And whenever this state occurs, it necessitates the cutting and division of those parts. And by this way, it became clear that the occurrence of the substance upon the contact of two substances is possible. And know: I have seen a group of affirmers of the indivisible substance who accepted the occurrence of the leap here. They claimed that alignment between them is only necessary if each of them moves along that distance. But if we say with the leap, that does not follow. Its exposition: if it is necessary in denying the indivisible substance to accept the leap, we also say: we accept it so that this question is repelled from us. As for the deniers of the leap, they said: By this proof it is established that the occurrence of the substance upon the contact of two substances is possible, and by it the second proof is validated, as previously. And God knows best.

Commentary
This passage combines three components: (1) The third aspect of the proof of possibility, which references the philosophers' third argument. (2) The philosophers' argument itself: a line of four atoms, with two parts placed above the ends and moving to the other side. For them to pass each other, alignment and opposition must occur at the conjunction of the second and third parts, forcing a division. (3) A discussion of the 'leap' (talfra) objection: some proponents of the indivisible atom admit a leap to avoid the conclusion of division, but opponents reject the leap and accept the proof as valid. The structure is: statement of the third aspect, presentation of the philosophical argument, and then the talfra controversy. The passage shows two responses within the atomist school: those who adopt the leap to evade the philosophers' conclusion, and those who reject the leap and consider the proof sound, thus supporting the possibility of one substance contacting two.

The Third Proof of the Philosophers and the Problem of Tafra
Razi presents the philosophers' third proof and the leap (tafra) response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third philosophical proof for the indivisible atom based on contact, and the response that invokes the concept of leap (tafra).

Core Idea
Contact and alignment force division, but the leap (tafra) offers an escape.

This passage presents a sophisticated argument by the philosophers to prove the existence of the indivisible atom (jawhar fard). It imagines a scenario involving moving atoms and contact, concluding that division must occur. However, a group of atomists respond by introducing the concept of 'leap' (tafra), which allows an atom to skip intermediate positions, thus avoiding contact. Let's explore this proof and its rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get the gist. Note the scenario with four parts and moving atoms.
The passage is dense; focus on understanding the setup first.
2
Trace the proof step-by-step
Understand the reasoning from placing parts to alignment and necessary division.
Pay attention to the terms 'mumāssa' and 'mulāqāt'.
3
Identify the leap response
See how the atomists avoid the conclusion by invoking tafra.
Tafra means skipping positions without traversing the intermediate distance.
4
Evaluate the counter-response
Consider the deniers of the leap argument that the proof still holds.
The deniers claim the proof remains valid even if some accept the leap.
5
Reflect on the implications
Think about how this proof and response relate to atomism and the debate over continuity.
This proof is one of several arguments for atomism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحويجة الثالثة للفلاسفة من الوجوه المبنية على المماسة والملاقاة : أن نقول : إذا ركبا خطاً من أربعة أجزاء ، ووضعنا فوق طرفـه الأيمن جزءاً ، ووضعنا فوق طرفه الأيمن جزءاً ، ووضعنا فوق طرفه الأيسر جزءاً آخر . ثم فرضنا : أنه ابتدءا هذان الجزء ان بالحركة، وانتهيا إلى آخر الخط دفعة . فهنا قد مر كل واحد من هذين الجزءين بصاحبه . ويمتنع أن يمر كل واحد منهما بصاحبه ، إلا إذا حصل التحاذي والتقابل بينهما. ومن المحال أن يحصل التحاذي والتقابل ، إلا على متصل الثاني والثالث . ومتى حصلت هذه [ الحالة (١) ] لزم القطع بوقوع القسمة والتجزئة في تلك الأجزاء . وبهذا الطريق ، ظهر أن وقوع الجوهر على متصل الجوهرين أمر ممكن جميع واعلم : أني رأيت جماعة من مثبتي الجوهر الفرد ، التزموا وقوع الطفرة ههنا. وزعموا : أن التحاذي بينهما ، إنما يجب لو تحرك كل واحد منها ، على تلك المسافة . أما إذا قلنا بالطفرة ، لم يلزم ذلك . وتقريره : أنه إذا كان لا بد في نفي الجوهر [ الفرد (۲) ] من التزام الطفرة . قلنا أيضاً : أن نلتزمها حتى يندفع عنا هذا السؤال . وأما المنكرون للطفرة ، فقالوا : ثبت بهذا البرهان أنه يمكن وقوع الجوهر على متصل الجوهرين ، وبه يصح البرهان الثاني . كما تقدم . والله أعلم
The third proof for the philosophers from the aspects based on touching and meeting: That we say: If we compose a line of four parts, and we place above its right end a part, and we place above its right end a part, and we place above its left end another part. Then we suppose that these two parts begin to move, and they reach the end of the line at once. So here each of these two parts has passed by its companion. And it is impossible for each of them to pass by its companion except if alignment and facing occur between them. And it is impossible for alignment and facing to occur except upon the contact of the second and third. And whenever this state occurs, it necessitates the certainty of the occurrence of division and partition in those parts. And by this way, it appears that the occurrence of the atom upon the contact of the two atoms is possible in all. And know: I have seen a group of affirmers of the indivisible atom who committed to the occurrence of leap (ṭafra) here. They claimed that alignment between them is necessary only if each of them moved along that distance. But if we say by the leap, that does not follow. And its explanation: If it is necessary in negating the [indivisible] atom to commit to the leap. We also say: we commit to it so that this question is repelled from us. As for the deniers of the leap, they said: it is established by this proof that the occurrence of the atom upon the contact of the two atoms is possible, and by it the second proof is valid. As has preceded. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents the third philosophical proof for the existence of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard), based on the concepts of contact (mumāssa) and meeting (mulāqāt). The proof imagines a line composed of four parts. A part is placed above the right end, another above the right end (likely a scribal duplication), and a third above the left end. Two of these parts move simultaneously towards the opposite ends. When they pass each other, they must at some point become aligned and face each other. This alignment can only occur if the moving parts come into contact with the intermediate parts (the second and third). Such contact necessitates division in those parts, proving that parts must be divisible and hence bodies are composed of atoms. The author then notes that some proponents of the indivisible atom respond by invoking the concept of ‘leap’ (ṭafra) — the idea that an atom can skip over intermediate positions without traversing them continuously. They argue that alignment is only required if movement is continuous; if a leap occurs, contact does not happen, so division does not follow. The author reports that advocates of the leap accept it to avoid the objection. Opponents of the leap, however, claim that this proof establishes the possibility of an atom’s occurrence on the contact point of two other atoms, thereby supporting the second proof. The passage concludes with ‘And God knows best’.

المماسة (mumāssa)
الملاقاة (mulāqāt)
التحاذي (taḥādhī)
التقابل (taqābul)
الطفرة (ṭafra)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the proof is decisive against atomism
Correction: The passage shows that the leap (ṭafra) provides a possible escape, so the proof is not conclusive.

Checkpoint

B) The infinite regress
C) The impossibility of motion
D) The distinction between essence and accident

Key Takeaway
The third proof uses contact to argue for division, but the leap (tafra) offers a way for atomists to avoid the conclusion.

The Fourth Proof: Sunlight and Atomic Surfaces
Razi presents three formulations of the fourth proof against atomism using sunlight on surfaces.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' fourth proof against atomism using sunlight on a surface and why it applies to all bodies, not just hypothetical atomic surfaces.

Core Idea
Light and shadow on a surface reveal that even supposed atoms must be divisible.

In this passage, Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents the fourth and final proof against the atomic theory of indivisible parts. The argument is elegantly simple: when sunlight falls on a surface, one side is illuminated and the other is not, implying a distinction that requires division. Razi offers three alternative formulations to reinforce the point, concluding that the proof applies to all sensible bodies, not just hypothetical atomic surfaces.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
This is the fourth of four proofs against atomism. It uses empirical observation of light and shadow to argue against indivisible parts.
Recall that atomism posits bodies composed of indivisible atoms.
2
First formulation: atomic surface
Imagine a surface made of atoms. When sunlight hits, one side is illuminated, the other dark. These sides are distinct, so the surface must have parts, contradicting indivisibility.
The key move: distinct properties imply division.
3
Second formulation: stacked surfaces
Consider a body as a stack of surfaces. The top surface has an upper side separate from other bodies and a lower side touching interior surfaces. These two sides differ, again requiring division.
This formulation uses mubāyana (separation) and mumāssa (touching).
4
Third formulation: real bodies
In any sensible body, when the sun shines, the illuminated side is one side of the top surface, while the other side lies in the depth. The distinction holds without assuming atoms.
The proof works for all bodies, strengthening the case.
5
Conclusion and significance
Razi states that this proof does not require a hypothetical atomic surface; it holds for all sensible bodies. This ends the four proofs presented.
The phrase 'to the fullest extent' indicates comprehensive treatment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : قالوا : إنا إذا فرضنا صفحة مركبة من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ ، ثم أشرقت الشمس عليها . فحينئذ يحصل الضوء في الوجه المقابل للشمس من ذلك السطح، وبقي الوجه الآخر منه غير مشرق . ومعلوم : : أن الوجه المشرق المضيء ، مغاير لما هو غير مشرق ولا مضيء ، وذلك يوجب الانقسام . ويمكن ذكر هذه الحجة بطريق آخر : فيقال : إن على القول بكون الجسم مركباً من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ ، يكون الجسم مؤلفاً من سطوح موضوعة ، بعضها على بعض . فالسطح الأعلى منها ، يكون بوجهه العالي مبايناً عن سائر الأجسام ، وبوجهه الأسفل يكون متصلا بالسطوح الداخلة في ذلك الجسم والوجه الذي به حصلت المباينة ، غير الوجه الذي [ به (۱) ] حصلت المماسة . وذلك يوجب حصول القسمة . ويمكن ذكره على طريق ثالث : فيقال : إن بتقدير كون الجسم مركباً من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ ، يكون الجسم مركباً من سطوح موضوعة بعضها على البعض . فإذا أشرقت الشمس على الجسم ، فقد استنار وجهه . وذلك الوجه عبارة عن أحد وجهي السطح الأعلى منه . وأما الوجه الثاني من ذلك السطح ، فإنه متصل بالسطح الأسفل منه ، وواقع في عمق ذلك الجسم. فيثبت : أن هذا البرهان لا حاجة في تقريره إلى وجود سطح مؤلف من الأجزاء التي لا تتجزأ ، بل هذا البرهان حاصل في جميع هذه الأجسام المحسوسة . فهذا هو الكلام في تقرير هذه البراهين الأربعة على أقصى الوجوه .
The fourth proof: They said: If we suppose a surface composed of parts that are indivisible, then the sun shines upon it. Then at that moment light occurs on the side facing the sun of that surface, and the other side of it remains not illuminated. And it is known: that the illuminated, bright side is distinct from that which is not illuminated nor bright, and that necessitates division. And this proof can be mentioned in another way: It is said: Upon the statement that a body is composed of indivisible parts, the body is composed of surfaces placed one upon another. The highest surface among them, with its upper side is separated from the rest of bodies, and with its lower side is connected to the surfaces inside that body. And the side by which separation occurs is other than the side by which touching occurs. And that necessitates the occurrence of division. And it can be mentioned in a third way: It is said: Given that a body is composed of indivisible parts, the body is composed of surfaces placed one upon another. So if the sun shines on the body, its side becomes illuminated. And that side is one of the two sides of its highest surface. As for the second side of that surface, it is connected to the lower surface, and lies in the depth of that body. So it is established: that this proof does not need in its establishment to the existence of a surface composed of indivisible parts, rather this proof holds in all these sensible bodies. This is the discussion in establishing these four proofs to the fullest extent.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof and its alternative formulations. The core argument: if a body is composed of indivisible parts (atoms), consider a surface of such a body when sunlight falls on it. One side becomes illuminated, the other remains dark. These two sides are distinct, implying that the surface has parts; thus the body is divisible. This contradicts the assumption of indivisibility. The author then offers two further formulations. In the second, he notes that the highest surface of a body has two sides: the upper side is separate from other bodies, the lower side touches interior surfaces. These two sides differ, requiring division. In the third, he states that when the sun shines, the illuminated side is one side of the top surface, while the other side is in the depth; this again shows distinction and division. He concludes that this proof does not require a hypothetical surface of atoms; it works for any sensible body. The phrase "this is the discussion in establishing these four proofs to the fullest extent" serves as a summary of the four proofs presented earlier.

Key Terms
الانقسام (al-inqisām)
السطح (al-saṭḥ)
الضوء (al-ḍaw')
المباينة (mubāyana)
المماسة (mumāssa)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The fourth proof only applies to a hypothetical surface made of indivisible parts.
Correction: Razi explicitly states the proof holds for all sensible bodies, not just a special atomic surface.

Checkpoint
According to the fourth proof, what does the difference between the illuminated and non-illuminated sides of a surface necessitate?
A) The surface is a single indivisible entity
B) The occurrence of division
C) The impossibility of light
D) The existence of a vacuum

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof uses observable light and shadow to demonstrate that even the smallest parts of a body must be divisible, refuting the atomist doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When the sun of truth shines on your beliefs, are there areas you keep in shadow because examining them would force you to admit they are divided or inconsistent? What would it take for you to turn that face toward the light today?
?
The atomist insisted on indivisible parts despite clear evidence of division. Is there a comfortable falsehood you refuse to let go because breaking it apart would be painful? Will you ask Allah to send the 'sunlight' of clear proof into that part of your heart, even if it shatters your assumptions?
?
The proof shows that light reveals hidden division. Your soul is illuminated by the Quran and revelation. Are you willing to examine your life under that light, exposing the places where your actions contradict your faith? Commit today to one specific area you will not allow to remain in darkness.
