The First Proof Against Hyle: The Three-Part Dilemma
Opponent presents first proof: body cannot have two parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first proof against the existence of hyle, which argues that a body cannot be composed of two parts by showing that all three logical possibilities are impossible.

Core Idea
If body had two parts, each would be a volume or not – all options fail.

This passage presents the first of several proofs against the existence of hyle (primordial matter). The proof is a classic dilemma: it assumes a body composed of two parts and then examines every possibility for what those parts could be. By showing each possibility leads to absurdity, the proof concludes that composition from hyle and form is impossible. As you read, notice how the argument uses the concept of volume (حجم) and the indivisible atom (جوهر فرد).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the three possibilities enumerated.
The passage uses technical terms like 'hyle' and 'volume'. Don't worry about definitions yet.
2
Identify the three possibilities
The argument presents three mutually exclusive possibilities for the two parts. Find them in the text and note how each is introduced with 'إما' (either).
The three cases are: both are volumes, one is a volume, or none is a volume.
3
Understand why each possibility fails
For each case, the text gives a reason why it is impossible. Try to follow the logic: the first case leads to containment of dimensions, the second leads to a self-subsistent substance or invalidates the indivisible atom, and the third is seemingly dismissed without explicit reasoning here.
The commentary explains the reasoning in more detail.
4
Connect to the conclusion
The argument concludes that 'the statement that the body is composed of hyle and form is invalid.' Reflect on how the three impossibilities together establish this conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث في الأدلة الدالة على نفي الهيولى احتج من قال بنفي الهيولى بوجوه : الحجة الأولى : إن الجسم لو كان مركباً في ماهيته من جزءين ، لكان لكل واحد منهما حقيقة وماهية باعتباره يمتاز عن الآخر إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : إما أن يكون كل واحد منهما من حيث إنه هو : حجماً . وإما أن يكون أحدهما حجماً ، والآخر ليس كذلك . وإما أن لا يكون واحد منهما حجماً . والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة ، فبطل القول بتركب الجسم من الهيولى والصورة . وأما أنه يمتنع كل واحد منهما : حجماً وممتداً في الحيز . فلأنهما لو كانا كذلك ، لزم كون أحد البعدين داخلا في الثاني . وذلك عندهم محال وأيضاً : فلما كان أحدهما محلاً للآخر ، وجب أن يكون ذلك المحل جوهراً قائماً بذاته ، فيكون الحجم على هذا التقدير جوهراً قائماً بالنفس . وأما القسم الثاني وهو أن يكون أحدهما حجماً دون الثاني . فإن قلنا : إن ما هو حجم في ذاته هو المحل - وما هو حجم في ذاته مراتب المثلثات - علمنا : أن هذا الشكل يبطل القول بإثبات الجوهر الفرد
Chapter Three: On the proofs indicating the denial of hyle. Those who deny hyle argued with several aspects: The first proof: If the body were composed in its quiddity of two parts, then each of them would have a reality and quiddity by virtue of which it is distinguished from the other. If you have understood this, we say: Either each of them, inasmuch as it is itself, is a volume; or one of them is a volume and the other is not; or neither of them is a volume. The three divisions are false, so the statement that the body is composed of hyle and form is invalid. As for the impossibility of each of them being a volume and extended in space, it is because if they were so, one of the dimensions would be contained within the second, and that is impossible according to them. Also: since one of them is a locus for the other, that locus must be a self-subsistent substance, so the volume on this assumption would be a self-subsistent substance. As for the second division, that one of them is a volume and the other not: if we say that what is a volume in itself is the locus, and what is a volume in itself is the ordering of triangles, we know that this figure invalidates the affirmation of the indivisible atom.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof against the existence of hyle (matter) from the perspective of those who deny it. The proof begins by assuming that if a body were composed of two parts in its quiddity, each part would have its own reality and quiddity distinguishing it from the other. Then three exhaustive possibilities for these parts are enumerated: both are volumes, one is a volume and the other is not, or neither is a volume. The proof argues that all three are impossible. The first case leads to one dimension being contained in another, which is impossible. Additionally, if one part is a locus for the other, the locus must be a self-subsistent substance, making volume itself a substance. The second case (one volume, one not) leads to a figure that invalidates the indivisible atom (jawhar fard). Thus the composition from hyle and form is refuted.

Key Terms
هيولى (hayula)
صورة (sura)
حجم (hajm)
جوهر (jawhar)
جوهر فرد (jawhar fard)
محال (muhal)
مركب (murakkab)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the second possibility considered in the first proof against hyle?
A) Both parts are volumes
B) One part is a volume, the other is not
C) Neither part is a volume
D) Both parts are immaterial

Key Takeaway
The first proof against hyle uses a trilemma: a body composed of two parts must have parts that are volumes or not, and all three options are impossible, thus refuting hyle-form composition.

Did you abandon it, or did you hold onto it despite the contradiction? Are you holding onto any such belief now? What would it take for you to let it go?

First Argument Against Hyle: Impossibility of Body Composition
First argument against hyle: three possibilities all impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first argument against the existence of hyle, which demonstrates that if a body were composed of two parts, all three logical possibilities are impossible.

Core Idea
Three logical possibilities for body composition, all impossible, refute hyle.

This lesson examines a central argument in Islamic atomism against the existence of hyle (matter) as a real component of bodies. The author argues that if a body were composed of two distinct parts, three possibilities arise — and each leads to absurdity. Understanding this logical refutation is key to grasping the Islamic rejection of Aristotelian hylomorphism.

Guided Path
1
Understand the premise
The argument begins by supposing that a body is composed of two parts in its essence. Each part would have its own reality distinguishing it from the other.
This is a hypothetical assumption to test the concept of hyle.
2
Identify the three possibilities
The author enumerates three logical possibilities: both parts are volumes, one is a volume and the other is not, or neither is a volume.
These cover all logical scenarios for the two parts.
3
See why each possibility fails
The author explains why the first two possibilities are impossible and implies the third is also false, leading to the conclusion that body cannot be composed of hyle and form.
The refutation of the second case refers to the ranks of triangles, which may be a corrupt phrase.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الأولى : إن الجسم لو كان مركباً في ماهيته من جزءين ، لكان لكل واحد منهما حقيقة وماهية. باعتباره يمتاز عن الآخر إذا عرفت هذا فنقول : إما أن يكون كل واحد منهما من حيث إنه هو : حجماً . وإما أن يكون أحدهما حجماً ، والآخر ليس كذلك . وإما أن لا يكون واحد منهما حجماً . والأقسام الثلاثة باطلة ، فبطل القول بتركب الجسم من الهيولى والصورة . أما أنه يمتنع كل واحد منهما : حجماً وممتداً في الحيز . فلأنهما لو كانا كذلك ، لزم كون أحد البعدين داخلا في الثاني . وذلك عندهم محال وأيضاً : فلما كان أحدهما محلاً للآخر ، وجب أن يكون ذلك المحل جوهراً قائماً بذاته ، فيكون الحجم على هذا التقدير جوهراً قائماً بالنفس . وأما القسم الثاني وهو أن يكون أحدهما حجماً دون الثاني . فإن قلنا : إن ما هو حجم في ذاته هو المحل - وما هو حجم في ذاته مراتب المثلثات - علمنا : أن هذا الشكل يبطل القول بإثبات الجوهر الفرد
The first proof: If the body were composed in its essence of two parts, each part would have a reality and quiddity distinguishing it from the other. If you understand this, we say: Either each one of them, insofar as it is itself, is a volume, or one of them is a volume and the other is not, or neither of them is a volume. The three divisions are false, so the claim that the body is composed of hyle and form is false. As for the impossibility that each of them be a volume and extended in space: because if they were so, then one of the dimensions would be included in the second, which is impossible according to them. Also, since one of them is a locus for the other, that locus must be a substance subsisting by itself, so the volume on this estimation would be a substance subsisting by itself. As for the second division—that one of them is a volume without the other: if we say that that which is a volume in itself is the locus—and that which is a volume in itself are the ranks of triangles—we know that this form invalidates the affirmation of the indivisible atom.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage presents the first argument against the existence of hyle (matter) by examining the composition of a body. The author states that if a body were composed of two parts in its quiddity, each part would have its own reality distinguishing it from the other. He then considers three possibilities: (1) both parts are volumes (i.e., extended in space), (2) one is a volume and the other is not, or (3) neither is a volume. He claims all three are impossible, thus the composition of body from hyle and form is false. He explains the first case: if both were volumes, one dimension would include the other, which is absurd, and one would be a locus for the other, making the volume a self-subsistent substance. The second case: if one is a volume without the other, that volume is the locus, and the ranks of triangles (perhaps a corrupt phrase) show that this form negates the atom. The third case is not elaborated here, but the argument is that all divisions fail, so composition is impossible.

Key Terms
الهيولى
الجسم
الجوهر الفرد
الحجم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is merely a theoretical exercise without practical implications.
Correction: The argument is intended to refute those who assert that hyle is a real principle of bodies, a key claim in Aristotelian physics.

Checkpoint

A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) One

Key Takeaway
The first argument against hyle shows that any composition of body from two parts must be impossible, thus body is not composed of hyle and form.

The Impossibility of Superposition (al-Tathiq)
Author argues against superposition, defends indivisible atom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the principle of superposition is rejected in Islamic atomism and how the author defends the indivisible atom against geometrical objections.

Core Idea
Superposition leads to contradiction: either partial division or wholesale loss of distinction.

This lesson tackles a central geometrical objection to atomism: the principle of superposition. The author argues that applying one line onto another leads to impossible consequences. Understanding this argument is key to grasping the rational defense of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two possibilities
The author considers two ways a line can meet another: partially or wholly. Understand each option.
Partial meeting implies divisibility; wholesale implies interpenetration.
3
Follow the reasoning against wholesale meeting
Trace the argument: if interpenetration occurs, distinction either remains or not. Both lead to absurdities.
Distinction cannot be by essence, concomitants, or accidents.
4
Examine the response to the objection
The author anticipates an objection about touching and meeting, and clarifies the only valid meaning.
Other meanings are imaginary and not reliable against decisive proofs.
5
Conclude the defense of atomism
The author concludes that superposition-based geometrical proofs do not undermine the decisive proofs for the indivisible atom.
This preserves atomism from geometrical criticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقي الأصل الثاني. وهو التطبيق: فنقول: هذا الأصل يعسر الطعن فيه. وإذا ثبتت صحته [ ثبت صحة (۱) ] ما تفرع عليه من هذه الدلائل والذي يمكن أن يقال فيه مع الاعتراف بأنه في غاية الصعوبة أن يقال: إنا لا نسلم إمكان تطبيق خط على خط، وسطح على سطح. والدليل عليه: أنا إذا طبقنا خطاً على خط آخر، فإما أن يلقاه ببعضه أو بكله. والأول يقتضي انقسام الخط في الطول، وهو محال. والثاني يوجب تفرد أحد الخطين في، بحيث تكون الإشارة إلى الآخر، وذلك محال. لأنه إذا حصل هذا النفوذ فههنا إما أن يبقى به الامتياز أو لا يبقى. والأول باطل. لأن الامتياز لا يمكن أن يقع بنفس الماهية. لأن الخطين مشتركان في تمام الماهية. ولا بلوازم الماهية، لأن لوازم الماهية مشترك بين أفراد الماهية، وما يكون مشتركاً فيه لا يكون موجباً بالامتياز ولا بالعوارض المفارقة. لأن كل عارض يفرض كونه عارضاً لأحدهما، فإنه لا بد وأن يكون عارضاً للآخر. لأنهما لما تداخلا ولم يتميز أحدهما عن الآخر بوجه من الوجوه. فكل عارض يوجد فإنه يكون نسبته إلى أحدهما، كنسبته إلى الآخر. فيكون ذلك العارض مشتركاً فيه. وما يكون مشتركاً فيه، لا يكون سبباً للامتياز. فثبت: أنه يمتنع امتياز أحد الخطين عن الآخر في نفس الأمر. وإذا لم يبق الامتياز، لزم إما اتحاد الاثنين وهو محال. أو أحدهما معاً، وهو أشد امتناعاً. فثبت: أن القول بالتطبيق يفضي إلى هذه الأقسام الباطلة، فوجب أن يكون القول به باطلا. فإن قالوا: فهذا الذي ذكرتم أن لا يماس شيء شيئاً، وأن لا يلقى شيء شيئاً. فنقول: قد ذكرنا في الدلائل المبنية على المماسة والملاقاة، أنه لا معنى لذلك لكون الشيئين متماسين، إلا حصولهما في حيزين، بحيث لا يحصل بينهما حيز فارغ، ولا شيء آخر. وأما ما سوى هذا المعنى في المماسة والملاقاة. فكل من الأمور الوهمية، والقضايا الظنية. وقد ثبت: أنه لما قامت الدلائل القاطعة الموجبة لنفيها، وجب أن لا يلتفت إلى حكم الظن والخيال. وذكرنا لهذا المعنى أمثلة كثيرة من مباحث الفلاسفة. فكذا ههنا الدلائل التي ذكرناها في إثبات الجوهر الفرد: دلائل قاطعة غير محتملة البتة. وهذه الدلائل الهندسية المذكورة، لما كانت مبنية على هذين الأصلين. أعني إثبات الدائرة وإثبات التطبيق، وكان الطعن فيهما، وإن كان بعيداً عن الوهم في الجملة: محتمل احتمالاً بعيداً، وجب المصير إليه، صوناً لتلك الدلائل القاطعة عن القدح والطعن. فهذا منتهى ما وصل إليه بحثنا في هذا. والله أعلم
The second principle remains: al-tathiq (superposition). So we say: This principle is difficult to object to. If its correctness is established, then what branches from it among these proofs is correct. What can be said about it, while acknowledging it is extremely difficult, is: we do not accept the possibility of applying a line to a line, or a surface to a surface. The proof of this is: If we apply a line to another line, then either it meets it partially or wholly. The first necessitates the division of the line in length, which is impossible. The second necessitates the penetration of one of the two lines into the other, such that there is no indication to the other, and that is impossible. Because if this penetration occurs, then either distinction (al-imtiyaz) remains or it does not. The first is false. Because distinction cannot occur by the essence (al-mahiyya) itself, since the two lines share the complete essence. Nor by the necessary concomitants (lawazim) of the essence, because the necessary concomitants of the essence are common among the individuals of the essence, and what is common does not cause distinction. Nor by accidental attributes (al-awarid al-mufariqa), because any accidental that is assumed to be an accident of one of them must also be an accident of the other. Since they interpenetrated and are not distinguished from each other in any way, every accidental that exists has the same relation to one as to the other. So that accidental is common, and what is common does not cause distinction. Thus it is established: it is impossible for one line to be distinguished from the other in actual fact. And if distinction does not remain, then either the two become one, which is impossible, or one of them becomes non-existent, which is even more impossible. Thus it is established: the statement of superposition leads to these false consequences, so the statement must be false. If they say: This that you have mentioned, that nothing touches anything and nothing meets anything? Then we say: We have already mentioned in the proofs based on touching (al-mumassa) and meeting (al-mulaqa) that the meaning of two things touching is nothing other than their occurrence in two loci such that there is no empty locus between them and no other thing. As for any other meaning of touching and meeting, it is among imaginary matters (al-umur al-wahmiyya) and probable propositions (al-qadaya al-zanniyya). And it is established: when the decisive proofs requiring their negation have been presented, it is necessary not to pay attention to the judgment of conjecture and imagination. And we have mentioned many examples of this from the investigations of the philosophers. Similarly here, the proofs we have mentioned for establishing the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard) are decisive proofs, absolutely not open to doubt. And these mentioned geometrical proofs, since they are based on these two principles—namely, the establishment of the circle and the establishment of superposition—and criticizing them, even if far from the imagination in general, is possible as a remote possibility, it is necessary to accept it, in order to protect those decisive proofs from criticism and objection. This is the utmost reached by our investigation on this matter. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a sustained argument against the principle of al-tathiq (superposition) and a defense of the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). The author first identifies two principles underlying the geometrical objections to atomism: the principle of the circle and the principle of superposition. Having already rejected the former, he now tackles the latter. He acknowledges that the principle of superposition is difficult to refute, but then presents a proof against it. The proof is: if we try to apply one line onto another, either they meet partially or wholly. Partial meeting requires infinite divisibility of the line, which is impossible for an atomist. Wholesale meeting implies interpenetration without distinction, leading to either the two becoming one or one annihilating the other—both absurd. Therefore superposition is impossible. The author anticipates an objection: what about touching and meeting? He responds that the only valid meaning of touching is spatial contiguity without a gap; any other meaning is imaginary and not to be relied upon against decisive proofs for the atom. He concludes that since the geometrical arguments rely on these two weak principles (circle and superposition), they do not undermine the definitive proofs for the indivisible atom.

Key Terms
التطبيق
الامتياز
الماهية
اللوازم
العوارض المفارقة
الجوهر الفرد
المماسة
الملاقاة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Superposition is a valid mathematical principle that can be freely used in geometry.
Correction: In the context of atomism, superposition leads to logical contradictions (division or loss of identity) and is therefore rejected.

Checkpoint
According to the argument, why is wholesale meeting (al-talaqi bi al-kull) of two lines impossible?
A) It requires the line to be divided.
B) It leads to interpenetration where distinction is lost, causing either unity or annihilation.
C) It is ruled out by the principle of the circle.
D) It is only possible in the imagination.

Key Takeaway
The principle of superposition is not a decisive proof against the indivisible atom, as it leads to logical absurdities that cannot be sustained.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you rely on intellectual arguments for your beliefs, are you willing to accept the remote possibility that some counterarguments might be valid in order to safeguard stronger proofs? How does that affect your certainty?
?
The author says that distinction cannot come from the shared essence. In your life, do you sometimes look for distinction in your own essence (identity) rather than in your actions? How can you shift to seeking distinction through what you do rather than who you are?
?
If you were presented with two equally plausible but contradictory positions, one supported by decisive proofs and the other by imaginative claims, would you have the courage to adopt the decisive one even if the alternative feels more intuitive? What is one area where you might be clinging to an imaginative claim?

Logic and Technical Terms
intermediate
6 min
Defending the Proof of the Indivisible Atom Against Geometrical Objections
The author defends the categorical proof of the indivisible atom against probable geometrical objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defends the categorical proof of the indivisible atom by distinguishing between certain and probable reasoning, and why geometrical objections based on probability do not undermine the proof.

Core Idea
Certain proofs trump probable objections.

In this passage, the author addresses a key challenge: how should we treat objections that are based on probable or imaginary notions when we already have categorical proofs? He argues that contact (mumāssa) should be understood in a precise way, and any other notion is merely probabilistic. Since the proofs for the indivisible atom are categorical, we must set aside merely probable geometrical objections to protect the certainty of the proof.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of contact
Read the author's definition of contact: two things in adjacent places with no gap. Note that other notions of contact are considered imaginary or probable.
This precise definition is key to the argument.
2
Recognize the hierarchy of proofs
The author distinguishes between categorical proofs (qāṭiʿa) and probable propositions (ẓanniyya). Categorical proofs necessitate acceptance regardless of probable objections.
This hierarchy is crucial for evaluating objections.
3
Apply the principle to geometrical objections
The geometrical objections are based on probable premises (like the circle and superposition). Since they are merely probable, they do not refute the categorical proof for the atom.
The author admits these objections are remotely possible but insists they must be set aside.
4
Reflect on the author's method
The author shows that protecting certain proofs from doubt sometimes requires accepting remote possibilities, but only to safeguard certainty.
This reflects a commitment to rational certainty over speculative doubt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك لكون الشيئين متماسين، إلا حصولهما في حيزين، بحيث لا يحصل بينهما حيز فارغ، ولا شيء آخر. وأما ما سوى هذا المعنى في المماسة والملاقاة. فكل من الأمور الوهمية، والقضايا الظنية. وقد ثبت: أنه لما قامت الدلائل القاطعة الموجبة لنفيها، وجب أن لا يلتفت إلى حكم الظن والخيال. وذكرنا لهذا المعنى أمثلة كثيرة من مباحث الفلاسفة. فكذا ههنا الدلائل التي ذكرناها في إثبات الجوهر الفرد: دلائل قاطعة غير محتملة البتة. وهذه الدلائل الهندسية المذكورة، لما كانت مبنية على هذين الأصلين. أعني إثبات الدائرة وإثبات التطبيق، وكان الطعن فيهما، وإن كان بعيداً عن الوهم في الجملة: محتمل احتمالاً بعيداً، وجب المصير إليه، صوناً لتلك الدلائل القاطعة عن القدح والطعن. فهذا منتهى ما وصل إليه بحثنا في هذا. والله أعلم
That is because two things being in contact means only that they occur in two places such that no empty space or anything else occurs between them. As for any other meaning of contact and meeting, all of these are imaginary matters and probable propositions. It has been established that when categorical proofs have been given that necessitate their negation, it is obligatory not to pay attention to the judgment of probability and imagination. We have mentioned many examples of this meaning from the investigations of the philosophers. Likewise here, the proofs we have mentioned for establishing the indivisible atom are categorical proofs, absolutely not subject to probability. As for these geometrical proofs that have been mentioned, since they are based on two principles — namely, establishing the circle and establishing superposition — and since the criticism against them, even if it is far from imagination in general, is possible in a remote way, it is necessary to adopt that criticism in order to protect those categorical proofs from objection and criticism. This is the extent of our research on this. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage concludes the discussion on the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard). It clarifies that contact (mumāssa) means two things occupying adjacent places with no gap, and any other notion of contact is merely imaginary (wahmī) or probable (zannī). Since categorical proofs (adilla qāṭiʿa) have established the atom, one must ignore probable judgments. The author notes that he has provided many examples from philosophical investigations. Then he addresses the geometrical objections based on the concepts of the circle and superposition. He admits that these objections, though remote from imagination, are remotely possible. Nevertheless, to safeguard the categorical proofs for the atom, one must accept those objections. This shows the author's commitment to rational certainty over probable speculation.

Key Terms

الدلائل القاطعة
المماسة
الملاقاة
الأمور الوهمية
القضايا الظنية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that any objection, however remote, suffices to refute a proof.
Correction: The author insists that only categorical proofs are decisive; remote probabilities do not overturn them.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why should geometrical objections to the indivisible atom be set aside?
A) They are based on false premises.
B) They are merely probable and cannot overturn categorical proofs.
C) They contradict the philosophers' consensus.
D) They are too complex to understand.

Key Takeaway
Categorical proofs for the indivisible atom are certain; merely probable geometrical objections do not undermine them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what area of your faith or life do you let remote doubts or probable objections prevent you from acting on clear truths? What specific step will you take this week to prioritize certainty over speculation?
?
When you face a doubt about a creedal matter, how do you determine whether it is a valid objection or an imaginary notion? Reflect on a time you entertained a remote possibility that weakened your conviction – what did you do?
?
The author says we must protect categorical proofs by adopting remote criticisms. Is there a certain belief you hold that you have not fully protected because you allow probable objections to linger? What is one truth you will reaffirm today, and how will you guard it against speculative doubts?
